Weed  \u00a0\t\t     Board of Directors Title: Member, Board of Directors (Term 2020 - 2024) Ward 4 Phone:  510-766-6075   Represents Ward 4   Email John Weed           Professional History John H. Weed is an attorney and also works in property development. He has military experience as a civil engineer and water utility consultant with the United States Air Force on installations worldwide. He retired as a Colonel with the U.S. Air Force Reserves in 2000. He was previously employed as an engineer technician with the Santa Clara Valley Water District and was the Special Assistant to the Division Manager of Ordnance Engineering at FMC Corporation. He currently serves on the Board of Directors of the Bay Area Water Supply and Conservation Agency and is an appointed member of the Alameda County Assessment Appeals Board. He is an active member of the California State Bar (88299). He was a member of the Board of Directors of the Association of California Water Agencies (ACWA) from 2005-2009, and is currently a Member of the ACWA Region 5 Council. Mr. Weed served as an elected Trustee of the Ohlone Community College District from 1977 to 2010 and has served as a Director of the Alameda County Water District since 1995. Educational History John has a bachelor\u2019s degree in civil engineering from the University of Santa Clara, a master\u2019s degree of business administration in finance from Eastern New Mexico University and doctoral level graduate studies at Water Resource Administration in University of Arizona. He obtained his Juris Doctor degree from the University of Santa Clara. \u00a0      Return to Previous Page                  Live Edit                                    About ACWD           Construction Projects           Development Services           Fish Passage & Related Projects           Groundwater Resources           Help on Tap Program           Optional Service Line Coverage Plan           Rapid Alert Notification System           Transparency Information           Water Rates Process                                                     My Account and Service                  Pay My Bill                  Transparency Information                                                          Board of Directors                  Your Water                  Job Seekers                                                                                                                              Contact Us                 Mailing Address: Alameda County Water District 43885 S Grimmer Boulevard Fremont, CA 94538 Business Hours:\u00a0 8 a.m. to 5 p.m.\u00a0 Lobby Hours:\u00a0 9 a.m. to 4 p.m. Monday - Friday (except holidays) Phone:  510-668-4200                                           Quick Links                 About ACWD's Conservation Program         Forms, Permits & Applications         Connect with Us         Services         Report Water Waste                     /QuickLinks.aspx                               Site Links                 Home         Site Map         Accessibility         Copyright Notices         Government Websites by CivicPlus\u00ae                     /QuickLinks.aspx                                                           For Water Emergencies Call:  510-668-6500                                                                                       Arrow Left         Arrow Right            []         Slideshow Left Arrow             Slideshow Right Arrow"}

Sethy  \u00a0\t\t     Board of Directors Title: Member, Board of Directors (Term 2022 - 2026) Ward 3 Phone:  510-789-5202   Represents Ward 3   Email Paul Sethy           Professional Experience Paul Sethy grew up in the City of Fremont and graduated from Mission San Jose High School.\u00a0 He then attended the University at Berkeley, School of Letters and Science, majoring in Economics and Business Administration. He is a career veteran of Silicon Valley's high technology industry and has worked in various product management positions for corporate leaders such as Verbatim, Xerox, 3Com, VeriFone and Hewlett-Packard.\u00a0 In more senior roles, he held full general management profit and loss responsibilities. In 1999, Mr. Sethy became the Founder, Chairman and CEO of AirPrime, Inc., for which he raised $82 million in venture capital financing during 2000-2001.\u00a0 The company eventually grew into a leading manufacturer of cellular modems for personal computers, smartphones, and industrial applications.\u00a0 The company also introduced the world's first internet capable smartphone in 2001, which was retailed by both Sprint and Verizon.\u00a0 AirPrime was later acquired by Sierra Wireless, a NASDAQ listed corporation (Stock Symbol: SWIR). Mr. Sethy was elected to the Board of Directors of the Alameda County Water District in 2010, and re-elected in 2014.\u00a0 Since joining the Board, he has served on the Board's Finance Committee, and has been the Chair since 2011. Additionally, he represents ACWD on the State Water Management, Local Government and Business Development Committees at the Association of California Water Agencies (ACWA).\u00a0 He also is an active member of the Alameda County Special Districts Association (ACSDA) and the California Special District Association (CSDA). In other civic engagements, and for many years, Mr. Sethy has been an active member of the Fremont Cultural Arts Council and Mission Peak Heritage Foundation, as well as a Board Member of the Washington Township Historical Society.\u00a0 He is also a long-time member of the Fremont Chamber of Commerce and serves on the Government Affairs Committee. \u00a0      Return to Previous Page                  Live Edit                                    About ACWD           Construction Projects           Development Services           Fish Passage & Related Projects           Groundwater Resources           Help on Tap Program           Optional Service Line Coverage Plan           Rapid Alert Notification System           Transparency Information           Water Rates Process                                                     My Account and Service                  Pay My Bill                  Transparency Information                                                          Board of Directors                  Your Water                  Job Seekers                                                                                                                              Contact Us                 Mailing Address: Alameda County Water District 43885 S Grimmer Boulevard Fremont, CA 94538 Business Hours:\u00a0 8 a.m. to 5 p.m.\u00a0 Lobby Hours:\u00a0 9 a.m. to 4 p.m. Monday - Huang  \u00a0\t\t     Board of Directors Title: Vice President, Board of Directors (Term 2022 - 2026) Ward 2 Phone:  510-299-4271   Represents Ward 2   Email Judy Huang           Professional History Judy C. Huang is a Registered Professional Engineer in California. She worked for the San Francisco Bay Region of the California Regional Water Quality Control Board as a Water Resource Control Engineer from 1993 to 1997 and as an Associate Water Resource Control Engineer from 1997 to 2006. She is currently an environmental engineer/project manager for the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency. Ms. Huang has served as a Director of the Alameda County Water District since 2002. Gunther  \u00a0\t\t     Board of Directors Title: President, Board of Directors (Term 2020 - 2024) Ward 1 Phone:  510-335-5791   Represents Ward 1   Email James Gunther           Professional History James G. Gunther is a professional engineer and currently serves as a supervisor for Transit America Services, Inc. He holds a Hazardous Materials Management Certificate and was formerly both a registered environmental assessor and a facility supervisor with an environmental cleanup and emergency response firm. He has 12 year of experience as a U.S. Coast Guard officer/engineer. Mr. Gunther has served as an active member of the Association of California Water Agencies since 1995 and has volunteered with the Fremont Fire Department, the Golden Gate National Recreation Area, and the Niles Canyon Railroad. Mr. Gunther has served as a Director of the Alameda County Water District since 1995. {"url": "https://www.acwd.org/720/Driscoll-Road-Main-Renewal-Project", "content": "Skip to Main Content                   Loading                                    Loading                    Do Not Show Again   Close                                                                                                                                           Search                             About Us Services Connect With Us I Want To...                                          Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program Driscoll Road Main Renewal Project                         Driscoll Road Main Renewal Project\t\t               Background The Driscoll Road Main Renewal Project is part of the District's Water Main Renewal Program and will improve systems hydraulics, seismic reliability, and post-earthquake service restoration, and will reduce maintenance costs by replacing the more than 60-year-old existing asbestos cement water main. The Project is located on Driscoll Road between Timber Creek Terrace and Mission Boulevard and on Paseo Padre Parkway between Gomes Road and Driscoll Road in Fremont (see  Project Location Map ). The Project will involve installing of approximately 1.5 miles of 12-inch and 16-inch diameter welded steel pipelines, associated fittings, valves, water service laterals, fire hydrants, and other appurtenances. Construction will commence at the beginning of 2024 and will be performed by Cratus, Inc., ACWD\u2019s appointed contractor. The project is anticipated to be completed in approximately 18 months. {"url": "https://www.acwd.org/594/Alvarado-Niles-Pipeline-Seismic-Improvem", "content": "Skip to Main Content                   Loading                                    Loading                    Do Not Show Again   Close                                                                                                                                           Search                             About Us Services Connect With Us I Want To...                                          Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program Alvarado Niles Pipeline Seismic Improvements                         Alvarado Niles Pipeline Seismic Improvements\t\t               Proposed Project Description: The Alvarado-Niles Pipeline Seismic Improvement Project is part of the District\u2019s $10 million per year Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program (MRSUP). This vital project will improve the seismic reliability of the water distribution systems in the northern portion of the Alameda County Water District\u2019s service area. The project will include the installation of over 3.5 miles of 14-inch and 16-inch steel pipe along Smith Street and Alvarado Niles Road, between Union City Boulevard and Decoto Road. This pipeline will be designed and installed to sustain a major seismic event along the Hayward Fault, and provide a critical water lifeline to our customers in the District\u2019s northern service area. Construction of the first phase was completed in July, 2021; construction of the second phase is planned for early 2024. Location Phase 2 - Smith Street at Union Pacific Railroad tracks, Alvarado Niles Road, between Santa Maria Drive and Almaden Boulevard, and between Central Avenue and Decoto Road. {"url": "https://www.acwd.org/456/Current-Fish-Passage-Related-Projects", "content": "Skip to Main Content                   Loading                                    Loading                    Do Not Show Again   Close                                                                                                                                           Search                             About Us Services Connect With Us I Want To...                                          Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Alameda Creek Fish Passage & Related Projects Current Fish Passage & Related Projects                         Current Fish Passage & Related Projects\t\t               Public Notices on Current Fish Passage & Related Projects Frequently Asked Questions Rubber Dam No. 1 & Flood Control Drop Structure Fish Ladder This project includes the design and installation of a fish ladder along the northern embankment of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel over ACWD\u2019s Rubber Dam No. 1 and the Alameda County Flood Control and Water Conservation District\u2019s (ACFCD) drop structure. This is a joint project between the ACFCD and ACWD. The fish ladder will help facilitate fish migration in the lower section of Alameda Creek. Location In the City of Fremont, within the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel at the flood control drop structure (BART weir) adjacent to the Quarry Lakes Regional Recreation Area. Location Map (PDF) Status The project is in the construction phase. See a  3D model of the fish ladder on YouTube. Funding To financially support this project the District has been awarded $2,500,000 by the California Department of Fish and Wildlife, $5,358,075 by the California Wildlife Conservation Board, and $500,000 by the National Fish and Wildlife Foundation. Commencement Anticipated Construction: Summer 2018 - Winter 2021 Project Manager: Shane O'Nesky Email Shane O'Nesky   Phone: 510-668-4489 Return to Current Projects page Shinn Pond Fish Screen This project includes the construction of new diversion pipelines and cylindrical fish screens that will replace the existing unscreened diversion pipes. The fish screen system will consist of several self-cleaning cylindrical screens with a track system on concrete pads along the bank of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel and will prevent juvenile steelhead trout from being trapped in Shinn Pond. The screened diversion facility will be used to divert water from the ACFCC to Shinn Pond. The project also includes security fencing, controls, and modification of the trail around the facility. Location In the City of Fremont, along the north side of the ACFCC upstream of Alameda County Water District Rubber Dam No. 1. Location Map (PDF) Status The project is in the construction phase. Funding To financially support this project the District has been awarded $2,945,000 by the California Department of Fish and Wildlife. A portion of the grant award was also used to fund the Kaiser Pond Fish Screen Project. {"url": "https://www.acwd.org/436/Completed-Fish-Passage-Related-Projects", "content": "Skip to Main Content                   Loading                                    Loading                    Do Not Show Again   Close                                                                                                                                           Search                             About Us Services Connect With Us I Want To...                                          Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Alameda Creek Fish Passage & Related Projects Completed Fish Passage & Related Projects                         Completed Fish Passage & Related Projects\t\t               Alameda Creek Pipeline No. 1 Fish Screen This project consisted of the installation of a fish screen that included multiple self-cleaning cylindrical fish screens, fencing, control panel and electrical boxes, and a section of new pipe that connected the fish screens pipe manifold to the existing Alameda Creek Pipeline No. 1 diversion pipe. The screen prevents juvenile steelhead trout from being carried into the diversion pipeline and adjacent groundwater recharge pond. Location In the City of Fremont, along the north side of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel between Mission Boulevard and the Union Pacific Railroad Bridge. Completion Date March, 2008 Funding The National Fish and Wildlife Foundation awarded $500,000 to the District as financial support for this project. Bunting Pond Fish Screen This project included modification of the water diversion intake and installation of a fish screen, fencing, control panel, and trail modification. The fish screen system consists of one self-cleaning cylindrical screen with a track system on a concrete pad along the bank of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel (ACFCC). The screen system and diversion intake is used to divert water from the ACFCC to Bunting Pond. The screen will prevent juvenile steelhead trout from being trapped in Bunting Pond. Location In the City of Fremont, along the south side of the ACFCC between the Union Pacific Railroad bridge and Alameda Water District Rubber Dam No. 3. Completion Date January, 2010 Funding The California Department of Water Resources awarded $600,000 to the District as financial support for this project. Rubber Dam No. 2 Decommissioning & Foundation Modification Project This project consisted of the removal of the fabric portion of the District's Rubber Dam No. 2 and the removal of a section of the dam's foundation to allow for fish passage in the lower portion of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel under low flow conditions. Location In the City of Fremont, within the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel adjacent to the Quarry Lakes Regional Recreational Area. Completion Date January, 2010 Funding The National Fish and Wildlife Foundation awarded 500,000 to the District as financial support for this project. Shinn Pond Gravity Rediversion Pipeline No. 2 The project consisted of installation of the 54-inch gravity rediversion pipeline with an intake structure in the bank of Shinn Pond, a flow metering vault, isolation gate valve and an outlet structure into Stevenson Pond. In addition, the project included the removal of Shinn Pond Pump Station and grout filling of the abandoned Rock Pond diversion pipeline between the Union Pacific Railroad and Bay Area Rapid Transit tracks. Completion Date February 2014 Kaiser Pond Fish Screen The project included the installation of 48-inch diversion pipeline and cylindrical fish screen to replace the existing unscreened diversion. The fish screen system consist of one self-cleaning cylindrical screen with a track system on a concrete pad along the bank of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel (ACFCC) to prevent juvenile steelhead trout from being trapped in Kaiser Pond. The screen system and diversion intake is used to divert water from the ACFCC to Kaiser Pond. Completion Date February 2014 Funding The District received $445,000 in financial support for this project from the California Department of Fish and Game Fisheries Restoration Grant Program. Rubber Dam No. 1 Fabric Replacement \u00a0 Rubber Dam No. 1 was installed in 1971 and is now approaching the end of its useful life. The replacement of Rubber Dam No. 1 will ensure the District's long term ability to maintain and improve the reliability of our critical water diversions from Alameda Creek to the Quarry Lakes Recreational Area for groundwater recharge.  The project will contain the following associated work: Replacement of the dam rubber (fabric) membrane element Replacement of existing dam anchorage Location In the City of Fremont, within the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel upstream of the BART weir and UPRR bridge. Location Map (PDF) Completion Date 2015 Return to Current Projects page Rubber Dam No. 3 Fish Ladder This project included the installation of a fish ladder along the northern embankment of the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel around ACWD's Rubber Dam No. 3. The fish ladder will help facilitate fish migration past the lower section of Alameda Creek. Location In the City of Fremont, within the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel in the vicinity of Mission Boulevard and the Union Pacific Railroad tracks. Location Map. (PDF) Funding To financially support this project the District has been awarded $3,000,000 from the California Natural Resources Agency, $500,000 from the National Fish and Wildlife Foundation, $825,000 from the State of California Coastal Conservancy, and $750,000 from the United States Bureau of Reclamation. Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Advanced Metering Infrastructure (AMI) Leak Detect Door Hanger                         Leak Detect Door Hanger\t\t                                                                     ACTION REQUIRED - LEAK DETECTED Your AMI meter could not be installed due to a pre-existing customer plumbing leak. The leak must be repaired before installation can take place. This is your first and only courtesy notice regarding the leak. Please call our installation hotline once resolved. ACWD\u2019s Board of Directors adopted an Ordinance (NO. 2008-01) Prohibiting Wasteful Use of Water, to conserve the District\u2019s water supply and eliminate the wasteful use of water, especially\u00a0 critical\u00a0 due\u00a0 to drought. Under this Ordinance leaks are required to be repaired as soon as possible, and\u00a0 ACWD can invoke the enforcement process for non-compliance. {"url": "https://www.acwd.org/751/AMI-Infographic", "content": "Skip to Main Content                   Loading                                    Loading                    Do Not Show Again   Close                                                                                                                                           Search                             About Us Services Connect With Us I Want To...                                          Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Advanced Metering Infrastructure (AMI) AMI Infographic                         AMI Infographic\t\t               Full-size infographic INVESTING IN OUR COMMUNITY \u00a0 The Alameda County Water District (ACWD) is investing in the future of our community by installing Advanced Metering Infrastructure (AMI), which allows water meters to be read remotely. While California is experiencing drought, ACWD plans decades in advance to ensure that our water supply remains reliable, and AMI is one action we are taking today to save water for tomorrow. \u00a0 HOW WILL THIS IMPACT YOU? Temporary Water Stoppage: \u00a0  Your water service will be temporarily turned off\u2014for no more than one hour unless otherwise communicated\u2014for the installation of the AMI device. If you have a water-dependent device (e.g., water recirculation pump), you will need to turn it off before your upgrade to avoid possible damage. \u00a0 \u00a0 Clear a Path: \u00a0 Please trim any overgrown landscaping or move any large objects near your water meter box to provide easy installer access. \u00a0 Pro Tip: Upgrading your water meter may cause temporary air in your pipes and water discoloration. Your water remains safe and meets or surpasses all state and federal drinking water standards for public health and safety. Please run water from a faucet without a screen for about 30 seconds to flush it out. Consider capturing this water for watering plants. \u00a0 WE\u2019LL NOTIFY YOU \u00a0 Check Your Mail\u00a0 Customers will receive a letter and email a few weeks in advance of your upgrade. \u00a0 Open Your Door\u00a0 Customers will receive a door hanger within 10 working days in advance of the work\u00a0 taking place and again once the work is completed.\u00a0 Go Online Visit ACWD.ORG/AMI for more information. Join us for a virtual community meeting on Nov. 16 at 6 p.m. to learn more about the AMI installation in your area. After installation, please share your feedback by taking a short, post-installation survey.\u00a0 ACWD began the AMI installation process in March 2021 and estimates each installation will take no longer than an hour. Full implementation in Fremont, Newark, and Union City will be complete by December 2023. The areas shown in blue on the above map have received AMI. \u00a0 MORE INSTALLATION DETAILS Our Team Our partners, Badger Meter and Professional Meters, Inc. (PMI) will upgrade or replace your water meter. We've also partnered with Utility Partners of America (UPA) to inspect our installations and ensure it meets our standards.\u00a0 \u00a0 Look for Our Team \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u2022 \u00a0 Neon green ACWD/PMI uniforms and branded vehicles \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u2022 \u00a0 Installers will carry a badge and letter to authenticate their work on the project \u00a0 You may see one of our quality control technicians during or after the installation \u00a0 CDC Guidelines Followed COVID-19 safety guidelines will be followed. \u00a0 WHY AMI? {"url": "https://www.acwd.org/738/Clean-Energy-Program", "content": "Skip to Main Content                   Loading                                    Loading                    Do Not Show Again   Close                                                                                                                                           Search                             About Us Services Connect With Us I Want To...                                          Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Clean Energy Program                         Multi Site Solar Photovoltaic Project\t\t               Clean Energy Program: Multi Site Solar Photovoltaic Project The District\u2019s Clean Energy Program will implement solar photovoltaic systems at several District facilities and properties. The program will be implemented over several fiscal years under Power Purchase Agreements (PPAs) with DG West 1, LLC, a solar developer and subsidiary of NextEra Energy Resources, LLC, in order to maximize value to the District while enhancing the environmental sustainability of the District\u2019s operations. The Clean Energy Program could reduce carbon emissions by over 2,000 tons annually and significantly reduce the District\u2019s energy costs over the life of the program. .\u00a0 \u00a0 Location:\u00a0 In the cities of Fremont and Newark, at several District-owned sites within the District\u2019s service area including ACWD\u2019s Headquarters, Desalination Facility, and covered reservoirs. \u00a0 Status:\u00a0 ACWD has executed PPAs with DG West 1, LLC for four (4) District-owned sites and is negotiating an agreement at two (2) additional sites. The first four are in design and are anticipated to be constructed and in operation by the end of 2023. Project Information Construction will be divided into two different phases to accommodate and coordinate with District Capital Improvements at the District-owned facilities included in this program. Phase 1 ACWD Headquarters Newark Desalination Facility Whitfield Reservoir Mayhew Reservoir \u00a0 Construction is scheduled for the second half of 2023. \u00a0 Phase 2 Alameda Reservoir Decoto Reservoir \u00a0 Construction is scheduled for the second half of 2024 through the second half of 2026. \u00a0 Project Engineer, Implementation Phase: Carlos Sempere Email:  carlos.sempere@acwd.com \u00a0                                                Advanced Metering Infrastructure (AMI)             Door Hanger #1           Door Hanger #2           Door Hanger #3           AMI Infographic           Leak Detect Door Hanger               Alameda Creek Fish Passage & Related Projects             Completed Fish Passage & Related Projects           Current Fish Passage & Related Projects               Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program             Alvarado Niles Pipeline Seismic Improvements           Driscoll Road Main Renewal Project           Small Diameter Pipeline Renewal Program               Kaiser Pond Diversion Pipe Improvement           Clean Energy Program           Curtner Road Booster Station Upgrade           Alameda Reservoir Roof Replacement Project           Groundwater PFAS Treatment Facility                                                     My Account and Service                  Pay My Bill                  Transparency Information                                                          Board of Directors                  Your Water                  Job Seekers                                                                                                                              Contact Us                 Mailing Address: Alameda County Water District 43885 S Grimmer Boulevard Fremont, CA 94538 Business Hours:\u00a0 8 a.m. to 5 p.m.\u00a0 Lobby Hours:\u00a0 9 a.m. to 4 p.m. Monday - Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Kaiser Pond Diversion Pipe Improvement                         Kaiser Pond Diversion Pipe Improvement\t\t               Kaiser Pond Diversion Pipe Improvement Project This groundwater recharge pond is divided by a levee along the Hayward Fault, which also divides the groundwater basin in two. The diversion pipe that allows water to flow from the east segment of the pond to the west is need of replacement. ACWD will construct a reinforced concrete box culvert through the levee to improve connectivity between the two segments. Location In the City of Fremont, adjacent to the Alameda Creek Flood Control Channel in the vicinity of Von Euw Common and the Union Pacific Railroad tracks. Map (PDF) Status Design of the Kaiser Pond Diversion Pipe Improvement Project is currently in progress. ACWD is in the progress of securing environmental permits. Home Services Capital Improvement Projects Current Projects Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program                         Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program (MRSUP)\t\t               As part of its commitment to delivering a reliable drinking water supply to more than 356,000 people living and working in Fremont, Newark, and Union City, the District implemented a District-wide Main Renewal and Seismic Upgrade Program (MRSUP). MRSUP projects include upgrading and seismically retrofitting water delivery pipelines and facilities. Intensive infrastructure upgrades will help improve water supply reliability for District customers in the event of a major earthquake and will reduce service interruptions due to aging pipelines.
